# Debug Q&A: Cilium eBPF Fault Isolation

**Repository:** cilium/cilium
**Task Type:** Debug Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Cilium is a Kubernetes CNI (Container Network Interface) plugin that uses eBPF (Extended Berkeley Packet Filter) programs to enforce network policies and route traffic. In a multi-node Kubernetes cluster, each node runs its own Cilium agent which compiles, loads, and attaches eBPF programs to enforce policies.

## Behavior Observation

**What happens:** When an eBPF program fails to compile or load on one Kubernetes node (e.g., due to a kernel verifier rejection, compilation error, or incompatible kernel features), the other nodes in the cluster continue to enforce their network policies normally. The failing node may log errors or degrade to a fallback mode, but the failure doesn't propagate cluster-wide.

**Why is this notable?** Many distributed systems that rely on shared state or centralized configuration can fail cluster-wide when one node encounters a problem. Cilium's architecture ensures that eBPF datapath failures are isolated to the affected node.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions to explain this behavior:

### Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle

How are eBPF programs compiled, loaded, and attached on each node independently?
- What component is responsible for compiling eBPF programs on each node?
- How does node-specific configuration (kernel version, enabled features, etc.) affect compilation?
- At what point in the lifecycle does the eBPF program become node-local vs. cluster-wide?

### Q2: Deployment Architecture

How does Cilium's deployment model ensure per-node isolation?
- How is the Cilium agent deployed across the cluster (DaemonSet, static pods, etc.)?
- What happens when one node's Cilium agent fails to initialize its eBPF programs?
- How does the control plane vs. data plane split contribute to isolation?

### Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement

Cilium network policies are cluster-wide resources (CRDs), but enforcement is per-node. How does this work?
- How are CiliumNetworkPolicy resources distributed to each node?
- What component on each node translates policies into eBPF bytecode?
- Why doesn't a compilation failure on one node block policy distribution to other nodes?

### Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation

eBPF programs use maps (hash tables, arrays) to store state. How is map state isolated across nodes?
- Are eBPF maps node-local or cluster-wide?
- What mechanisms (BPF filesystem pinning, namespaces) ensure map isolation?
- If a node fails to create or update a map, how does that affect other nodes' packet processing?

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:

```
# Cilium eBPF Fault Isolation

## Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and function references>

## Q2: Deployment Architecture
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and function references>

## Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and function references>

## Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation
<answer with specific file paths, class names, and function references>

## Evidence
<consolidated list of supporting file paths and line references>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT modify any source files
- Cite specific files, classes, and functions — avoid vague or speculative answers
- Focus on the `pkg/datapath/loader/`, `pkg/policy/`, `pkg/maps/`, and `pkg/endpoint/` directories

862026-03-08T22:19:52.712876agentmessage-
The investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here is a summary of the findings:

---

## Summary of Findings

### Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle

**Compilation component:** The `loader` struct in `pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go` is responsible. It invokes `clang` as a subprocess via `compile()` (`compile.go:170`). The higher-level `compileDatapath()` (`compile.go:266`) selects `bpf_lxc.c` (endpoint) or `bpf_host.c` (host endpoint).

**Node-specific configuration:** Before compilation, the agent writes two C header files containing node-specific values: `node_config.h` (via `WriteNodeConfig()` in `pkg/datapath/linux/config/config.go:104`) embedding the node's IPs, CIDRs, identity constants, and feature flags; and `netdev_config.h`. The kernel's BPF ISA support is probed at runtime via `getBPFCPU()` (`compile.go:135`), which calls `probes.HaveV2ISA()`/`HaveV3ISA()` and passes `-mcpu=v1/v2/v3` to clang. The `objectCache` hashes the full node config (SHA-256) to detect when recompilation is needed.

**Node-local from the start:** The ELF is compiled to a per-endpoint state directory on the local filesystem, loaded into the local kernel's verifier, and attached to local network interfaces. BPF maps are pinned to the node's `/sys/fs/bpf` — never shared across nodes.

### Q2: Deployment Architecture

Cilium is deployed as a **DaemonSet** (`daemonset.yaml:16`), guaranteeing one agent per node. Each pod uses `hostNetwork: true` and mounts the host's `/sys/fs/bpf`. When one node's agent fails to initialize eBPF, the `orchestrator.reconciler()` (`orchestrator.go:146`) retries after 10 seconds and marks health as `Degraded` — entirely local. The `dpInitialized` channel blocks that node's endpoint builds but has no effect on other nodes. The control plane

It will block if multiple\n   163  // threads attempt to concurrently fetchOrCompile a template binary for the\n   164  // same set of EndpointConfiguration.\n   165  //\n   166  // Returns a copy of the compiled and parsed ELF and a hash identifying a cached entry.\n   167  func (o *objectCache) fetchOrCompile(ctx context.Context, nodeCfg *datapath.LocalNodeConfiguration, cfg datapath.EndpointConfiguration, dir *directoryInfo, stats *metrics.SpanStat) (spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, hash string, err error) {\n   168          cfg = wrap(cfg)\n   169\n   170          hash, err = o.baseHash.hashTemplate(o, nodeCfg, cfg)\n   171          if err != nil {\n   172                  return nil, \"\", err\n   173          }\n   174\n   175          // Capture the time spent waiting for the template to compile.\n   176          if stats != nil {\n   177                  stats.BpfWaitForELF.Start()\n   178                  defer func() {\n   179                          // Wrap to ensure that \"err\" is compared upon return.\n   180                          stats.BpfWaitForELF.End(err == nil)\n   181                  }()\n   182          }\n   183\n   184          scopedLog := log.WithField(logfields.BPFHeaderfileHash, hash)\n   185\n   186          // Only allow a single concurrent compilation per hash.\n   187          obj := o.serialize(hash)\n   188          defer obj.Unlock()\n   189\n   190          // The serialize call might have blocked for a significant amount of time\n   191          // if another compilation was in progress. Make sure that the endpoint is\n   192          // still alive, to bail out early otherwise, and prevent doing unnecessary\n   193          // operations that would likely fail.\n   194          select {\n   195          case <-ctx.Done():\n   196                  return nil, \"\", ctx.Err()\n   197          default:\n   198          }\n   199\n   200          if obj.spec != nil {\n   201                  return obj.spec.Copy(), hash, nil\n   202          }\n   203\n   204          if stats == nil {\n   205                  stats = &metrics.SpanStat{}\n   206          }\n   207\n   208          path, err := o.build(ctx, nodeCfg, cfg, stats, dir, hash)\n   209          if err != nil {\n   210                  if !errors.Is(err, context.Canceled) {\n   211                          scopedLog.WithError(err).Error(\"BPF template object creation failed\")\n   212                  }\n   213                  return nil, \"\", err\n   214          }\n   215\n   216          obj.spec, err = bpf.LoadCollectionSpec(path)\n   217          if err != nil {\n   218                  return nil, \"\", fmt.Errorf(\"load eBPF ELF %s: %w\", path, err)\n   219          }\n   220\n   221          return obj.spec.Copy(), hash, nil\n   222  }"

"// regenerateBPF rewrites all headers and updates all BPF maps to reflect the\n// specified endpoint.\n// ReloadDatapath forces the datapath programs to be reloaded. It does\n// not guarantee recompilation of the programs.\n// Must be called with endpoint.mutex not held and endpoint.buildMutex held.\n//\n// Returns the policy revision number when the regeneration has called,\n// Whether the new state dir is populated with all new BPF state files,\n// and an error if something failed.\nfunc (e *Endpoint) regenerateBPF(regenContext *regenerationContext) (revnum uint64, reterr error) {\n        var err error\n\n        stats := &regenContext.Stats\n        stats.waitingForLock.Start()\n\n        datapathRegenCtxt := regenContext.datapathRegenerationContext\n\n        // Wait for the datapath to be initialized before we take the compilation read lock.\n        // If we take the read lock before the datapath is initialized, we end up blocking\n        // the datapath initialization which needs the write lock on `e.compilationLock`.\n        // Yet, we will be blocked while waiting for the initialization to finish, thus causing\n        // a deadlock.\n        <-e.owner.Orchestrator().DatapathInitialized()\n\n        // Make sure that owner is not compiling base programs while we are\n        // regenerating an endpoint.\n        e.owner.GetCompilationLock().RLock()\n        stats.waitingForLock.End(true)\n        defer e.owner.GetCompilationLock().RUnlock()\n\n        if err := e.aliveCtx.Err(); "// regeneratePolicy computes the policy for the given endpoint based off of the\n// rules in regeneration.Owner's policy repository.\n//\n// Policy generation may fail, and in that case we exit before actually changing\n// the policy in any way, so that the last policy remains fully in effect if the\n// new policy can not be implemented. "// UpdatePolicy triggers policy updates for all live endpoints.\n// Endpoints with security IDs in provided set will be regenerated. Otherwise, the endpoint's\n// policy revision will be bumped to toRev.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) UpdatePolicy(idsToRegen *set.Set[identity.NumericIdentity], fromRev, toRev uint64) {\n        eps := mgr.GetEndpoints()\n\n        wg := sync.WaitGroup{}\n        wg.Add(len(eps))\n\n        for _, ep := range eps {\n                go func(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) {\n                        ep.UpdatePolicy(idsToRegen, fromRev, toRev)\n                        wg.Done()\n                }(ep)\n        }\n\n        wg.Wait()\n}"

"func (e *Endpoint) UpdatePolicy(idsToRegen *set.Set[identityPkg.NumericIdentity], fromRev, toRev uint64) {\n        // no deferred unlocks here, as we must\n        // release locks before regenerating\n\n        e.buildMutex.Lock() // buildMutex is required to update policy revision\n        if err := e.lockAlive(); err != nil {\n                e.buildMutex.Unlock()\n                return\n        }\n\n        unlock := func() {\n                e.unlock()\n                e.buildMutex.Unlock()\n        }\n\n        secID := e.getIdentity()\n        if secID == identityPkg.InvalidIdentity {\n                unlock()\n                return\n        }\n\n        // If this endpoint's security ID has a policy update, we must regenerate. Otherwise,\n        // bump the policy revision directly (as long as we didn't miss an update somehow).\n        if !idsToRegen.Has(secID) {\n                if e.policyRevision < fromRev {\n                        // FIXME: https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/36493\n                        // Currently policy repository version can be bumped through multiple triggers\n                        // async to each other. This can lead to out of order processing of regeneration\n                        // events. Continue with endpoint regeneration to be safe but log as Info.\n                        e.getLogger().WithField(logfields.PolicyRevision, fromRev).Info(\"Endpoint missed a policy revision; triggering regeneration\")\n                } else {\n                        e.getLogger().WithField(logfields.PolicyRevision, toRev).Debug(\"Policy update is a no-op, bumping policyRevision\")\n                        e.setPolicyRevision(toRev)\n\n                        unlock()\n                        return\n                }\n        }\n\n        // Policy change affected this endpoint's identity; queue regeneration\n        regenMetadata := &regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata{\n                Reason:            \"policy rules updated\",\n                RegenerationLevel: regeneration.RegenerateWithoutDatapath,\n        }\n        regen := e.setRegenerateStateLocked(regenMetadata)\n        unlock()\n\n        if regen {\n                <-e.Regenerate(regenMetadata)\n        }\n}\n\n// RegenerateIfAlive queue a regeneration of this endpoint into the build queue\n// of the endpoint and returns a channel that is closed when the regeneration of\n// the endpoint is complete. The channel returns:\n//   - false if the regeneration failed\n//   - true if the regeneration succeed\n//   - nothing and the channel is closed if the regeneration did not happen\nfunc (e *Endpoint) RegenerateIfAlive(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) <-chan bool {\n        regen, err := e.SetRegenerateStateIfAlive(regenMetadata)\n        if err != nil {\n                log.WithError(err).Debugf(\"Endpoint disappeared while queued to be regenerated: %s\", regenMetadata.Reason)\n        }\n        if regen {\n                // Regenerate logs status according to the build success/failure\n                return e.Regenerate(regenMetadata)\n        }\n\n        ch := make(chan bool)\n        close(ch)\n        return ch\n}"

  "file_text": "# Cilium eBPF Fault Isolation\n\n## Q1: Per-Node eBPF Lifecycle\n\n### Component Responsible for Compilation\n\nEach node runs its own **Cilium agent** (a Go binary, `cilium-agent`), which owns the entire eBPF lifecycle locally. The compilation subsystem lives in `pkg/datapath/loader/`. The central type is `loader` (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:74`), which wraps an `objectCache` (`pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go:27`) and a `compilationLock` (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:86`).\n\nCompilation is performed by invoking `clang` as a subprocess. The entry point is `compile()` in `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go:170`, which builds a `clang` command line and runs it via `exec.WithCancel`. The higher-level function `compileDatapath()` (`compile.go:266`) selects either `bpf_lxc.c` (endpoint programs) or `bpf_host.c` (host endpoint programs) and calls `compile()`. Overlay, WireGuard, XDP, and network programs each have their own compile helpers (`compileOverlay`, `compileWireguard`, `compileNetwork`, `compileAndLoadXDPProg`).\n\n### How Node-Specific Configuration Affects Compilation\n\nBefore any compilation, the agent writes two node-specific C header files:\n\n1. **`node_config.h`** \u2014 written by `loader.writeNodeConfigHeader()` (`base.go:63`), which calls `HeaderfileWriter.WriteNodeConfig()` (`pkg/datapath/linux/config/config.go:104`). This embeds the node's IPv4/IPv6 addresses, CIDR allocations, identity constants, MTU, enabled features, and dozens of other node-local values as `#define` macros.\n\n2. **`netdev_config.h`** \u2014 written by `loader.writeNetdevHeader()` (`base.go:46`), which calls `WriteNetdevConfig()` (`config.go:982`). This encodes per-node option flags.\n\nThe CPU ISA target is also probed at runtime: `getBPFCPU()` (`compile.go:135`) calls `probes.HaveV3ISA()` and `probes.HaveV2ISA()` (`pkg/datapath/linux/probes/probes.go:406,420`) to detect the kernel's BPF ISA support and passes `-mcpu=v1/v2/v3` to `clang`. The number of possible CPUs (`-D__NR_CPUS__`) is also injected at compile time (`compile.go:191`).\n\nThe `objectCache` hashes the full node configuration via `hashDatapath()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/hash.go:17`), which SHA-256s the output of `WriteNodeConfig`. If the hash changes (e.g., after a node IP change), `UpdateDatapathHash()` (`cache.go:58`) invalidates all cached compiled objects and forces recompilation.\n\n### When the eBPF Program Becomes Node-Local\n\nThe program is node-local from the moment `clang` is invoked on that node. The compiled ELF object is written to a per-endpoint state directory under `option.Config.StateDir/<endpoint-id>/` (`pkg/endpoint/directory.go:35`). After loading via `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` (`pkg/bpf/collection.go:236`), the kernel verifier runs on that node's kernel. The resulting BPF programs are then attached to the node's network interfaces via `attachSKBProgram()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/tc.go:26`) using TC or TCX hooks. BPF maps are pinned to the node's BPF filesystem at `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/` or `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/` (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go:51,57`). None of this state is shared with or visible to other nodes.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: Deployment Architecture\n\n### DaemonSet Deployment\n\nCilium is deployed as a Kubernetes **DaemonSet** (`install/kubernetes/cilium/templates/cilium-agent/daemonset.yaml:16`). Kubernetes guarantees exactly one agent pod per node. Each pod runs with `hostNetwork: true` (`daemonset.yaml:771`) and mounts the host's BPF filesystem at `/sys/fs/bpf` (`daemonset.yaml:308,814`). An init container ensures the BPF filesystem is mounted before the agent starts (`daemonset.yaml:594`).\n\n### What Happens When One Node's Agent Fails to Initialize eBPF\n\nThe `orchestrator` (`pkg/datapath/orchestrator/orchestrator.go:69`) drives the initialization loop. Its `reconciler()` goroutine (`orchestrator.go:146`) calls `reinitialize()` (`orchestrator.go:256`), which calls `loader.Reinitialize()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/base.go:382`). If `Reinitialize()` returns an error, the orchestrator logs a warning, marks its health as `Degraded`, and schedules a retry after `reinitRetryDuration` (10 seconds) (`orchestrator.go:209-213`). The `dpInitialized` channel (`orchestrator.go:73`) is only closed after the first successful initialization; all endpoint regenerations block on this channel (`orchestrator.go:305-312`), so a failing node simply stalls its own endpoint builds without affecting other nodes.\n\nIf a specific endpoint's BPF program fails to compile or load, `realizeBPFState()` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:566`) returns the error, which propagates up through `regenerateBPF()` (`bpf.go:379`). The endpoint's `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` (`pkg/endpoint/policy.go:908`) catches the failure via `regenFailedChan` and retries regeneration with exponential back-off using a controller (`RunInterval: 1s, ErrorRetryBaseDuration: 2s`). The endpoint is marked degraded locally; other nodes are unaffected.\n\n### Control Plane vs. Data Plane Split\n\nThe **control plane** (policy distribution, identity allocation, endpoint management) runs in the Cilium agent process and communicates with the Kubernetes API server and optionally a KV store (etcd). The **data plane** (packet forwarding, policy enforcement) runs entirely in eBPF programs attached to the node's kernel. These two planes are decoupled: the control plane can continue receiving policy updates from the API server even if the data plane fails to load. The `compilationLock` (`pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go:430`) is a node-local read-write mutex that serializes base program compilation against endpoint regeneration on the same node only (`daemon/cmd/daemon.go:204`). No cross-node locking exists.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement\n\n### How CiliumNetworkPolicy Resources Are Distributed\n\nEach Cilium agent independently watches the Kubernetes API server for `CiliumNetworkPolicy` (CNP) and `CiliumClusterwideNetworkPolicy` (CCNP) resources using a `policyWatcher` (`pkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go:26`). The watcher is started per-agent via the `Cell` lifecycle hook (`pkg/policy/k8s/cell.go:43,125`). It uses `resource.Resource[*cilium_v2.CiliumNetworkPolicy]` \u2014 a typed informer/reflector \u2014 to receive add/update/delete events from the API server. Each agent maintains its own local `cnpCache` (`watcher.go:56`).\n\n### Component That Translates Policies into eBPF Bytecode\n\nThe translation pipeline is:\n\n1. **`policyWatcher.onUpsert()`** (`pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go:23`) receives a CNP event, parses it via `cnp.Parse()`, and calls `policyImporter.UpdatePolicy()` (`cilium_network_policy.go:153`).\n\n2. **`policyImporter.processUpdates()`** (`pkg/policy/cell/policy_importer.go:263`) applies the rules to the node-local `policy.Repository` via `repo.ReplaceByResource()`, then calls `endpointManager.UpdatePolicy()` (`policy_importer.go:382`).\n\n3. **`endpointManager.UpdatePolicy()`** (`pkg/endpointmanager/manager.go:852`) iterates over all local endpoints and calls `ep.UpdatePolicy()` on each, which queues a regeneration event.\n\n4. **`Endpoint.regenerate()`** \u2192 **`regenerateBPF()`** \u2192 **`realizeBPFState()`** (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:566`) calls `orchestrator.ReloadDatapath()`, which calls `loader.ReloadDatapath()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:700`).\n\n5. **`objectCache.fetchOrCompile()`** (`pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go:167`) either retrieves a cached compiled ELF or calls `compileDatapath()` to invoke `clang`. The resulting ELF is loaded into the kernel via `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` and attached to the endpoint's veth interface.\n\n6. **`selectorPolicy.DistillPolicy()`** (`pkg/policy/resolve.go:160`) converts the selector-based `selectorPolicy` into a concrete `EndpointPolicy` with a `policyMapState` (map of identity+port+direction \u2192 allow/deny). This is then synced to the per-endpoint `cilium_policy_v2_<id>` BPF map via `policyMapSync()` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:521`).\n\n### Why a Compilation Failure on One Node Doesn't Block Other Nodes\n\nPolicy distribution (steps 1\u20133 above) is entirely in userspace and does not depend on BPF compilation succeeding. The `policyImporter` applies rules to the in-memory `Repository` and signals endpoint regeneration regardless of whether the BPF load succeeds. Each node's `Repository` is a completely independent in-memory data structure (`pkg/policy/repository.go:160`). A compilation failure on node A returns an error from `realizeBPFState()` on node A only; node B's `policyImporter` and `Repository` are separate processes with separate goroutines and separate BPF filesystems. There is no shared compilation state, no distributed lock, and no cross-node error propagation path.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation\n\n### Are eBPF Maps Node-Local or Cluster-Wide?\n\nAll eBPF maps used by Cilium are **node-local**. They are created by the Cilium agent process on each node and pinned to that node's BPF filesystem. There is no mechanism for BPF maps to span kernel boundaries across nodes.\n\n### BPF Filesystem Pinning and Namespaces\n\nMaps are pinned to the BPF filesystem (`bpffs`) mounted at `/sys/fs/bpf` (default, `pkg/defaults/defaults.go:96`) or `/run/cilium/bpffs` (fallback). The `CheckOrMountFS()` function (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go:295`) ensures the filesystem is mounted at agent startup.\n\nMap pin paths follow a strict per-node hierarchy:\n\n- **Global maps** (shared across all endpoints on a node): `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/<mapname>` \u2014 e.g., `cilium_lxc`, `cilium_ct4_global`, `cilium_ipcache`. Path computed by `MapPath()` (`bpffs_linux.go:98`).\n- **Per-endpoint maps**: `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/<mapname><endpoint-id>` \u2014 e.g., `cilium_policy_v2_00042`. Path computed by `LocalMapPath(name, id)` (`bpffs_linux.go:112`), which calls `LocalMapName()` (`bpffs_linux.go:107`) to format the name as `<prefix><5-digit-id>`.\n- **Per-endpoint bpf_link pins**: `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/endpoints/<endpoint-id>/links/` \u2014 used for TCX attachment. Path computed by `bpffsEndpointLinksDir()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/paths.go:73`).\n- **Per-device bpf_link pins**: `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/devices/<device>/links/` \u2014 for host/netdev programs. Path computed by `bpffsDeviceLinksDir()` (`paths.go:44`).\n\nThe `CollectionOptions.Maps.PinPath` field is set to `bpf.TCGlobalsPath()` when loading programs (`loader.go:517`), which causes the `cilium/ebpf` library to automatically pin all maps in the ELF to that directory on the node's bpffs.\n\nConnection tracking maps can be either global (`cilium_ct4_global`, `cilium_ct6_global`) or per-endpoint (`cilium_ct4_<id>`, `cilium_ct6_<id>`) depending on the `ConntrackLocal` option (`pkg/endpoint/endpoint.go:894`, `pkg/maps/ctmap/ctmap.go:820-828`).\n\n### How a Map Failure on One Node Affects Other Nodes\n\nIf a node fails to create or update a BPF map, the error is returned from `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` (`pkg/bpf/collection.go:236`) or from a map update call. This error propagates up through `reloadEndpoint()` or `reloadHostEndpoint()` \u2192 `ReloadDatapath()` \u2192 `realizeBPFState()` \u2192 `regenerateBPF()`, where it is logged and the endpoint is marked as failed on that node only. The `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` controller retries the operation locally.\n\nOther nodes' BPF maps are pinned to their own `/sys/fs/bpf` instances (each node has its own kernel and its own bpffs mount). A map creation failure on node A cannot affect the map state on node B because:\n\n1. BPF maps are kernel objects \u2014 they exist only in the kernel of the node that created them.\n2. The bpffs is a per-node filesystem; it is not a network filesystem.\n3. The Cilium agent on each node creates and manages its own maps independently, with no cross-node coordination for map operations.\n\nPacket processing on node B continues uninterrupted using node B's existing BPF maps, even if node A's agent is completely unable to load any BPF programs.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### pkg/datapath/loader/\n\n| File | Key References |\n|------|---------------|\n| The compilation subsystem lives in `pkg/datapath/loader/`. The central type is `loader` (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:74`), which wraps an `objectCache` (`pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go:27`) and a `compilationLock` (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:86`).\n\nCompilation is performed by invoking `clang` as a subprocess. The entry point is `compile()` in `pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go:170`, which builds a `clang` command line and runs it via `exec.WithCancel`. The higher-level function `compileDatapath()` (`compile.go:266`) selects either `bpf_lxc.c` (endpoint programs) or `bpf_host.c` (host endpoint programs) and calls `compile()`. Overlay, WireGuard, XDP, and network programs each have their own compile helpers (`compileOverlay`, `compileWireguard`, `compileNetwork`, `compileAndLoadXDPProg`).\n\n### How Node-Specific Configuration Affects Compilation\n\nBefore any compilation, the agent writes two node-specific C header files:\n\n1. **`node_config.h`** \u2014 written by `loader.writeNodeConfigHeader()` (`base.go:63`), which calls `HeaderfileWriter.WriteNodeConfig()` (`pkg/datapath/linux/config/config.go:104`). This embeds the node's IPv4/IPv6 addresses, CIDR allocations, identity constants, MTU, enabled features, and dozens of other node-local values as `#define` macros.\n\n2. **`netdev_config.h`** \u2014 written by `loader.writeNetdevHeader()` (`base.go:46`), which calls `WriteNetdevConfig()` (`config.go:982`). This encodes per-node option flags.\n\nThe CPU ISA target is also probed at runtime: `getBPFCPU()` (`compile.go:135`) calls `probes.HaveV3ISA()` and `probes.HaveV2ISA()` (`pkg/datapath/linux/probes/probes.go:406,420`) to detect the kernel's BPF ISA support and passes `-mcpu=v1/v2/v3` to `clang`. The number of possible CPUs (`-D__NR_CPUS__`) is also injected at compile time (`compile.go:191`).\n\nThe `objectCache` hashes the full node configuration via `hashDatapath()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/hash.go:17`), which SHA-256s the output of `WriteNodeConfig`. If the hash changes (e.g., after a node IP change), `UpdateDatapathHash()` (`cache.go:58`) invalidates all cached compiled objects and forces recompilation.\n\n### When the eBPF Program Becomes Node-Local\n\nThe program is node-local from the moment `clang` is invoked on that node. The compiled ELF object is written to a per-endpoint state directory under `option.Config.StateDir/<endpoint-id>/` (`pkg/endpoint/directory.go:35`). After loading via `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` (`pkg/bpf/collection.go:236`), the kernel verifier runs on that node's kernel. The resulting BPF programs are then attached to the node's network interfaces via `attachSKBProgram()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/tc.go:26`) using TC or TCX hooks. BPF maps are pinned to the node's BPF filesystem at `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/` or `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/` (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go:51,57`). None of this state is shared with or visible to other nodes.\n\n---\n\n## Q2: Deployment Architecture\n\n### DaemonSet Deployment\n\nCilium is deployed as a Kubernetes **DaemonSet** (`install/kubernetes/cilium/templates/cilium-agent/daemonset.yaml:16`). Kubernetes guarantees exactly one agent pod per node. Each pod runs with `hostNetwork: true` (`daemonset.yaml:771`) and mounts the host's BPF filesystem at `/sys/fs/bpf` (`daemonset.yaml:308,814`). An init container ensures the BPF filesystem is mounted before the agent starts (`daemonset.yaml:594`).\n\n### What Happens When One Node's Agent Fails to Initialize eBPF\n\nThe `orchestrator` (`pkg/datapath/orchestrator/orchestrator.go:69`) drives the initialization loop. Its `reconciler()` goroutine (`orchestrator.go:146`) calls `reinitialize()` (`orchestrator.go:256`), which calls `loader.Reinitialize()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/base.go:382`). If `Reinitialize()` returns an error, the orchestrator logs a warning, marks its health as `Degraded`, and schedules a retry after `reinitRetryDuration` (10 seconds) (`orchestrator.go:209-213`). The `dpInitialized` channel (`orchestrator.go:73`) is only closed after the first successful initialization; all endpoint regenerations block on this channel (`orchestrator.go:305-312`), so a failing node simply stalls its own endpoint builds without affecting other nodes.\n\nIf a specific endpoint's BPF program fails to compile or load, `realizeBPFState()` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:566`) returns the error, which propagates up through `regenerateBPF()` (`bpf.go:379`). The endpoint's `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` (`pkg/endpoint/policy.go:908`) catches the failure via `regenFailedChan` and retries regeneration with exponential back-off using a controller (`RunInterval: 1s, ErrorRetryBaseDuration: 2s`). The endpoint is marked degraded locally; other nodes are unaffected.\n\n### Control Plane vs. Data Plane Split\n\nThe **control plane** (policy distribution, identity allocation, endpoint management) runs in the Cilium agent process and communicates with the Kubernetes API server and optionally a KV store (etcd). The **data plane** (packet forwarding, policy enforcement) runs entirely in eBPF programs attached to the node's kernel. These two planes are decoupled: the control plane can continue receiving policy updates from the API server even if the data plane fails to load. The `compilationLock` (`pkg/datapath/loader/compile.go:430`) is a node-local read-write mutex that serializes base program compilation against endpoint regeneration on the same node only (`daemon/cmd/daemon.go:204`). No cross-node locking exists.\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Policy Distribution vs. Enforcement\n\n### How CiliumNetworkPolicy Resources Are Distributed\n\nEach Cilium agent independently watches the Kubernetes API server for `CiliumNetworkPolicy` (CNP) and `CiliumClusterwideNetworkPolicy` (CCNP) resources using a `policyWatcher` (`pkg/policy/k8s/watcher.go:26`). The watcher is started per-agent via the `Cell` lifecycle hook (`pkg/policy/k8s/cell.go:43,125`). It uses `resource.Resource[*cilium_v2.CiliumNetworkPolicy]` \u2014 a typed informer/reflector \u2014 to receive add/update/delete events from the API server. Each agent maintains its own local `cnpCache` (`watcher.go:56`).\n\n### Component That Translates Policies into eBPF Bytecode\n\nThe translation pipeline is:\n\n1. **`policyWatcher.onUpsert()`** (`pkg/policy/k8s/cilium_network_policy.go:23`) receives a CNP event, parses it via `cnp.Parse()`, and calls `policyImporter.UpdatePolicy()` (`cilium_network_policy.go:153`).\n\n2. **`policyImporter.processUpdates()`** (`pkg/policy/cell/policy_importer.go:263`) applies the rules to the node-local `policy.Repository` via `repo.ReplaceByResource()`, then calls `endpointManager.UpdatePolicy()` (`policy_importer.go:382`).\n\n3. **`endpointManager.UpdatePolicy()`** (`pkg/endpointmanager/manager.go:852`) iterates over all local endpoints and calls `ep.UpdatePolicy()` on each, which queues a regeneration event.\n\n4. **`Endpoint.regenerate()`** \u2192 **`regenerateBPF()`** \u2192 **`realizeBPFState()`** (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:566`) calls `orchestrator.ReloadDatapath()`, which calls `loader.ReloadDatapath()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/loader.go:700`).\n\n5. **`objectCache.fetchOrCompile()`** (`pkg/datapath/loader/cache.go:167`) either retrieves a cached compiled ELF or calls `compileDatapath()` to invoke `clang`. The resulting ELF is loaded into the kernel via `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` and attached to the endpoint's veth interface.\n\n6. **`selectorPolicy.DistillPolicy()`** (`pkg/policy/resolve.go:160`) converts the selector-based `selectorPolicy` into a concrete `EndpointPolicy` with a `policyMapState` (map of identity+port+direction \u2192 allow/deny). This is then synced to the per-endpoint `cilium_policy_v2_<id>` BPF map via `policyMapSync()` (`pkg/endpoint/bpf.go:521`).\n\n### Why a Compilation Failure on One Node Doesn't Block Other Nodes\n\nPolicy distribution (steps 1\u20133 above) is entirely in userspace and does not depend on BPF compilation succeeding. The `policyImporter` applies rules to the in-memory `Repository` and signals endpoint regeneration regardless of whether the BPF load succeeds. Each node's `Repository` is a completely independent in-memory data structure (`pkg/policy/repository.go:160`). A compilation failure on node A returns an error from `realizeBPFState()` on node A only; node B's `policyImporter` and `Repository` are separate processes with separate goroutines and separate BPF filesystems. There is no shared compilation state, no distributed lock, and no cross-node error propagation path.\n\n---\n\n## Q4: eBPF Map Scoping and State Isolation\n\n### Are eBPF Maps Node-Local or Cluster-Wide?\n\nAll eBPF maps used by Cilium are **node-local**. They are created by the Cilium agent process on each node and pinned to that node's BPF filesystem. There is no mechanism for BPF maps to span kernel boundaries across nodes.\n\n### BPF Filesystem Pinning and Namespaces\n\nMaps are pinned to the BPF filesystem (`bpffs`) mounted at `/sys/fs/bpf` (default, `pkg/defaults/defaults.go:96`) or `/run/cilium/bpffs` (fallback). The `CheckOrMountFS()` function (`pkg/bpf/bpffs_linux.go:295`) ensures the filesystem is mounted at agent startup.\n\nMap pin paths follow a strict per-node hierarchy:\n\n- **Global maps** (shared across all endpoints on a node): `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/<mapname>` \u2014 e.g., `cilium_lxc`, `cilium_ct4_global`, `cilium_ipcache`. Path computed by `MapPath()` (`bpffs_linux.go:98`).\n- **Per-endpoint maps**: `/sys/fs/bpf/tc/globals/<mapname><endpoint-id>` \u2014 e.g., `cilium_policy_v2_00042`. Path computed by `LocalMapPath(name, id)` (`bpffs_linux.go:112`), which calls `LocalMapName()` (`bpffs_linux.go:107`) to format the name as `<prefix><5-digit-id>`.\n- **Per-endpoint bpf_link pins**: `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/endpoints/<endpoint-id>/links/` \u2014 used for TCX attachment. Path computed by `bpffsEndpointLinksDir()` (`pkg/datapath/loader/paths.go:73`).\n- **Per-device bpf_link pins**: `/sys/fs/bpf/cilium/devices/<device>/links/` \u2014 for host/netdev programs. Path computed by `bpffsDeviceLinksDir()` (`paths.go:44`).\n\nThe `CollectionOptions.Maps.PinPath` field is set to `bpf.TCGlobalsPath()` when loading programs (`loader.go:517`), which causes the `cilium/ebpf` library to automatically pin all maps in the ELF to that directory on the node's bpffs.\n\nConnection tracking maps can be either global (`cilium_ct4_global`, `cilium_ct6_global`) or per-endpoint (`cilium_ct4_<id>`, `cilium_ct6_<id>`) depending on the `ConntrackLocal` option (`pkg/endpoint/endpoint.go:894`, `pkg/maps/ctmap/ctmap.go:820-828`).\n\n### How a Map Failure on One Node Affects Other Nodes\n\nIf a node fails to create or update a BPF map, the error is returned from `bpf.LoadAndAssign()` (`pkg/bpf/collection.go:236`) or from a map update call. This error propagates up through `reloadEndpoint()` or `reloadHostEndpoint()` \u2192 `ReloadDatapath()` \u2192 `realizeBPFState()` \u2192 `regenerateBPF()`, where it is logged and the endpoint is marked as failed on that node only. The `startRegenerationFailureHandler()` controller retries the operation locally.\n\nOther nodes' BPF maps are pinned to their own `/sys/fs/bpf` instances (each node has its own kernel and its own bpffs mount). A map creation failure on node A cannot affect the map state on node B because:\n\n1. BPF maps are kernel objects \u2014 they exist only in the kernel of the node that created them.\n2. The bpffs is a per-node filesystem; it is not a network filesystem.\n3. The Cilium agent on each node creates and manages its own maps independently, with no cross-node coordination for map operations.\n\nPacket processing on node B continues uninterrupted using node B's existing BPF maps, even if node A's agent is completely unable to load any BPF programs.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### pkg/datapath/loader/\n\n| File | Key References |\n|------|---------------|\n|
